   628	        }
   629	
   630	        /// <summary>
   631	        /// Base58Check encode (Bitcoin-style: payload || SHA256(SHA256(payload))[0:4]).
   632	        /// Upstream: <c>bs58check.ts bs58check.encode</c>.
   633	        /// </summary>
   634	        public static string Base58CheckEncode(byte[] payload)
   635	        {
   636	            if (payload == null)
   637	            {
   638	                throw new ArgumentNullException(nameof(payload));
   639	            }
   640	            using (var sha = SHA256.Create())
   641	            {
   642	                var h1 = sha.ComputeHash(payload);
   643	                var h2 = sha.ComputeHash(h1);
   644	                var checksum = new byte[4];
   645	                Array.Copy(h2, 0, checksum, 0, 4);
   646	                var concat = new byte[payload.Length + 4];
   647	                Array.Copy(payload, 0, concat, 0, payload.Length);
   648	                Array.Copy(checksum, 0, concat, payload.Length, 4);
   649	                return Base58Encode(concat);
   650	            }
   651	        }
   652	
   653	        /// <summary>
   654	        /// Base58Check decode (Bitcoin-style). Verifies the trailing 4-byte
   655	        /// SHA256(SHA256(payload)) checksum.
   656	        /// Upstream: <c>bs58check.ts bs58check.decode</c>.
   657	        /// </summary>
   658	        public static byte[] Base58CheckDecode(string encoded)
   659	        {
   660	            byte[] decoded = Base58Decode(encoded);
   661	            if (decoded.Length < 4)
   662	            {
   663	                throw new ArgumentException("Invalid Base58Check string - too short");
   664	            }
   665	
   666	            var data = new byte[decoded.Length - 4];
   667	            Array.Copy(decoded, 0, data, 0, data.Length);
   668	            var checksum = new byte[4];
   669	            Array.Copy(decoded, decoded.Length - 4, checksum, 0, 4);
   670	
   671	            using (var sha = SHA256.Create())
   672	            {
   673	                var h1 = sha.ComputeHash(data);
   674	                var h2 = sha.ComputeHash(h1);
   675	                if (h2[0] != checksum[0] || h2[1] != checksum[1]
   676	                    || h2[2] != checksum[2] || h2[3] != checksum[3])
   677	                {
   678	                    throw new ArgumentException("Invalid Base58Check checksum");
   679	                }
   680	            }

    20

    49	## Re-pinning procedure
    50	
    51	When bumping any pin:
    52	
    53	1. Update the table above (npm version, refresh tarball sha256, gitHead).
    54	2. Update `Directory.Packages.props` or any version comment.
    55	3. Re-run `npm pack` and refresh the extracted directories under
    56	   `upstream-snapshots/`.
    57	4. Re-run **3 Codex review rounds per affected file** via
    58	   [`codex-crypto-review.sh`](./codex-crypto-review.sh).
    59	5. Update `CHANGELOG.md`.

     1	# Codex multi-round crypto review
     2	
     3	This directory holds the evidence that proves the C# implementation is a 1:1
     4	logical port of the Turnkey TypeScript SDK at the **peak-pinned versions**.
     5	
     6	## SOP
     7	
     8	For each of the 6 production files under `src/`:
     9	
    10	1. `Encoding.cs`
    11	2. `CryptoConstants.cs`
    12	3. `Crypto.cs`
    13	4. `ApiKeyStamper.cs`
    14	5. `Http.cs`
    15	6. `TurnkeyJsonContext.cs`
    16	
    17	run **three independent rounds** of Codex review using
    18	[`codex-crypto-review.sh`](./codex-crypto-review.sh). Each round writes a
    19	separate evidence file named `{file}.cs-r{N}-{YYYYMMDD}.md`.
    20	
    21	A file is considered "review-clean" only when round 3 reports:
    22	
    23	- section B has zero `NOT-REVIEWED` rows (or each NOT-REVIEWED row has a
    24	  documented justification),
    25	- section D states "no banned API present" (Crypto.cs only),
    26	- section E has zero entries,
    27	- section F states "all fixtures match".
    28	
    29	## Pinned upstream sources
    30	
    31	The authoritative upstream sources are the npm tarballs extracted under
    32	[`upstream-snapshots/`](./upstream-snapshots/). The exact tarball sha256 is in
    33	[`upstream-snapshots/tarball-checksums.txt`](./upstream-snapshots/tarball-checksums.txt).
    34	
    35	GitHub commit SHAs are recorded in [`turnkey-source-pins.md`](./turnkey-source-pins.md)
    36	as **secondary** metadata only. The npm tarball is the source of truth because
    37	npm publish contents may differ from the git tree (excluded test files,
    38	included build output, etc.).
    39	
    40	## Unity port reference
    41	
    42	The pre-existing C# Unity port at
    43	[`packages/turnkey-sdk-unity/Runtime/`](../packages/turnkey-sdk-unity/Runtime/)
    44	(peak submodule SHA in [`unity-source-pins.md`](./unity-source-pins.md)) is used
    45	**only as a C# adaptation reference**. Logic divergence from the peak-pinned
    46	TS source must be resolved by re-porting from the TS source, not by trusting
    47	the Unity port.
    48	
    49	## Codex prompt template
    50	
    51	Codex is invoked with the following prompt (sections A-G required in every
    52	review round; pass criterion in `codex-crypto-review.sh`):
    53	
    54	```
    55	SYSTEM:
    56	You are reviewing a C# port of the Turnkey TypeScript SDK file: {cs-file}
    57	The pinned upstream npm tarball is at:
    58	  codex-crypto-reviews/upstream-snapshots/turnkey-{pkg}-{version}/
    59	  (sha256 in tarball-checksums.txt — record the matching hash in your output)
    60	The C# file is at:
    61	  src/{cs-file}
    62	
    63	REQUIRED OUTPUTS for this review round (all must appear in your output):
    64	
    65	A. Source pin acknowledgement: upstream package name, version, tarball sha256
    66	   (from tarball-checksums.txt), C# file's `git rev-parse HEAD` SHA.
    67	
    68	B. Method coverage table: every public + internal helper method in {cs-file}
    69	   listed in a markdown table:
    70	     - C# method (file:line)
    71	     - Upstream TS function (path:line within upstream-snapshots/...)
    72	     - Status: REVIEWED / NOT-REVIEWED
    73	     - Notes (one line)
    74	   Do NOT skip a row. If upstream counterpart is missing, set NOT-REVIEWED.
    75	
    76	C. Intentional adaptations: every C#/TS pattern adaptation explicitly listed
    77	   with the reason why it is structural (does not change wire bytes or
    78	   observable behavior). Examples: Task<T>↔Promise<T>, byte[]↔Uint8Array,
    79	   BouncyCastle X↔noble Y, System.Text.Json↔JSON.stringify, BigInteger↔BigInt,
    80	   exceptions↔Error/throw.
    81	
    82	D. (Crypto.cs only) D17 enforcement check: confirm BouncyCastle is used only
    83	   for ECDSA / ECDH / AES-GCM / SHA-256 / HMAC / BigInteger / EC point ops.
    84	   The following MUST NOT appear in Crypto.cs:
    85	     - Org.BouncyCastle.Crypto.Generators.HkdfBytesGenerator
    86	     - Org.BouncyCastle.Crypto.Hpke.*
    87	     - Any "high-level" KDF or HPKE wrapper
    88	   If any banned API is present, flag it as a divergence.
    89	
    90	E. Logic divergence findings: every place where C# behavior differs from
    91	   upstream TS in any of:
    92	     - algorithm step order
    93	     - constant values
    94	     - error handling (which condition throws what)
    95	     - byte ordering
    96	     - leading-zero handling
    97	     - padding
    98	     - rounding / normalization
    99	     - signature format (DER vs raw r||s, low-S)
   100	     - DTO shape (field names, order, presence, optionality)
   101	     - JSON serialization (property order, casing, null handling, escaping)
   102	   For each: C# file:line, TS upstream-snapshots/...:line, semantic difference,
   103	   suggested fix.
   104	
   105	F. Fixture comparison gate: for every test fixture that touches this file
   106	   (in tests/Fixtures/), confirm it was generated from the pinned upstream
   107	   package and the C# test asserts the same bytes Node produces.
   108	
   109	G. Unresolved assumptions you could not verify.
   110	
   111	PASS criterion: B has zero NOT-REVIEWED rows (or documented justifications)
   112	AND E has zero entries AND D is "no banned API present" AND F is
   113	"all fixtures match".
   114	
   115	DO NOT use phrases like "looks good" or "no divergence found" without
   116	producing sections A–F.
   117	```

   120

   909	
   910	## User preferences
   911	
   912	- when composing the `turnkey-sdk-csharp` `/goal`, the visible constraint was "create the repository under `KyuzanInc`, private, and do not update the current `peak` repository" -> keep standalone repo work isolated from `peak` unless the user explicitly asks for a cross-repo change [Task 1]
   913	
   914	## Reusable knowledge
   915	
   916	- The early repo-bootstrap pattern used upstream package snapshots and generated lock/docs artifacts rather than hand-porting from memory: `Directory.Packages.props`, `global.json`, `README.md`, `turnkey-sdk-csharp.sln`, `src/Turnkey.Sdk/Turnkey.Sdk.csproj`, `tests/Turnkey.Sdk.Tests/Turnkey.Sdk.Tests.csproj`, `tests/packages.lock.json`, and snapshot trees such as `snapshots/turnkey-http-3.16.0/...` were all part of the visible scaffold [Task 1]
   917	- The target quality bar was strict functional alignment with the original Turnkey Node.js / TypeScript package logic, with `turnkey-sdk-unity` and upstream snapshots used as mapping/reference material rather than as the final authority [Task 1][Task 2]
   918	- The first high-value parity surface was `Encoding.cs`: preserve Unity-specific helpers only where needed, but explicitly port behavior for helpers equivalent to base64, `pointEncode`, `hexToAscii`, `normalizePadding`, and `bs58Check encode`, backed by upstream test vectors and parity tests [Task 2]
   919	
   920	## Failures and how to do differently
   921	
   922	- Symptom: the new C# port "works" for common cases but diverges from upstream on edge cases. Cause: direct C# rewrites missed TypeScript semantics in length handling, malformed/odd hex parsing, and base64url invalid-character handling. Fix: add upstream-style fixtures first, then patch `Encoding.cs` until parity tests pass [Task 2]
   923	- Symptom: the agent drifts into modifying `peak` while preparing the new repo. Cause: the plan file lived in `peak`, but the deliverable was a separate repository. Fix: keep `peak` as planning/reference context only and do implementation work inside `turnkey-sdk-csharp` [Task 1]

PR-14 should conditionally depend on PR-9b if PR-7a passes (`plans/...:529`, `534`). |

No conflict with `FINAL-INTEGRATED-REVIEW-20260523.md` on the main review-clean claim: that file says GO at lines 1-3 and notes exact HTTP fixtures are deferred at lines 43-47. The fixture provenance scheme matches `tests/Fixtures/README.md:6-16`. The stamper and HTTP reconciliation docs support the plan’s future Node generator direction (`ApiKeyStamper...:87-101`, `Http...:67-78`), but not the inconsistent drift/HPKE wording above.

**C. Cryptographic Claim Audit**

Corrections required.

1. HPKE/QOS: pinned `@turnkey/crypto@2.8.8` has SDK HPKE functions with RFC 9180 JSdoc at `crypto.ts:87-156`, and QOS is a separate `quorumKeyEncrypt` path at `crypto.ts:218-275`. The C# port is the SDK HPKE path (`src/Crypto.cs:404-456`), not QOS. Correction: remove remaining “Turnkey HPKE = QOS spec” wording at plan lines 179-182 and 663.

2. HPKE AEAD: upstream `SUITE_ID_2` is `HPKE 0x0010 0x0001 0x0002` (`constants.ts:1-2`), and `crypto.ts` derives a 32-byte key (`crypto.ts:129-135`, `337-343`). Correction: replace AES-128-GCM with AES-256-GCM in plan lines 72 and 406-407.

3. Noble low-S deterministic path: upstream `purejs.ts` calls `p256.sign(hash, input.privateKey)` at lines 21-23, but the package only declares `@noble/curves` as `^1.3.0` at `package.json:50-53`, not an exact tarball-pinned v1.3.0. The plan’s PR-4 exact lock and preflight assertion at lines 332-336 is therefore load-bearing and should remain.

4. Stamper JSON order and scheme: confirmed. `index.ts` constructs `{ publicKey, scheme, signature }` in that order and uses `SIGNATURE_SCHEME_TK_API_P256` at `index.ts:94-102`.

5. Published tarballs exclude tests/fixtures: confirmed. Package `files` only include `dist/`, `CHANGELOG.md`, `README.md` for crypto (`package.json:30-34`), api-key-stamper (`36-40`), http (`33-37`), and encoding (`26-30`). Local `find` over `package/` found no `__tests__`, `__fixtures__`, `*test*`, or `*fixture*`.

**D. Coverage / Scope**

PR-3 scope is bounded but larger than the plan’s compressed table suggests. Concrete upstream test names requiring C# add/map/N/A include:

- Api-key-stamper point/sign/stamp: `pointDecode -> uncompressed invalid`, `pointDecode -> uncompressed valid`, `pointDecode -> compressed`, `sign with Turnkey fixture: sign (node crypto)`, `sign with Turnkey fixture: sign (WebCrypto)`, `sign with Turnkey fixture: sign (PureJS)`, `sign with Turnkey fixture: sign (universal)`, `sign with openssl generated key pairs: stamp (node)`, `stamp (WebCrypto)`, `stamp (universal)`, `uses provided signature to make stamp`.
- Crypto: HPKE auth, HPKE standard, decryptExportBundle mnemonic/non-mnemonic, getPublicKey, generateP256KeyPair, compressRawPublicKey, decryptCredentialBundle, extractPrivateKeyFromPKCS8Bytes, verifyRequestStamp, uncompress happy/invalid prefix/invalid length, session JWT verification.
- DER parser exact 14 tests: the two valid DER tests at `crypto-test.ts:263-282` plus the twelve invalid/edge tests at `287-454`.
- Proof N/A/provenance-only: four proof tests at `proof-tests.ts:63-101`.
- HTTP: six `withAsyncPolling` tests at `async-test.ts:43-274`, plus `requests are stamped after initialization` and `requests return grpc status details as part of their errors`.
- Encoding: five index tests at `index-test.ts:15-116`.

Primitive omissions: for current C# public surface, no major Turnkey-used primitive is missing after v3 adds Ed25519, secp256k1, Base58Check, AES-GCM, SHA-256, HMAC-SHA256, HKDF, and ECDSA. SHA-512 is QOS-only (`crypto.ts:223`, `792-844`) and QOS is out of scope. P-384/SHA-384 appear in proof certificate verification (`proof.ts:39-45`, `276`), but proof implementation is explicitly deferred.

PR-11 fixture seeding is not harmful if `ProofFixtureProvenanceTests` lands in the same PR. It is harmful only if the FAQ wording at lines 609-611 is followed literally and JSON is committed with no consumer at all.

**E. Operational Risk**

Existing CI workflows do not set up Node and do not invoke generators. `ci.yml` only sets up .NET and runs `dotnet test` (`ci.yml:19-22`, `41-44`); `release.yml` also sets up .NET and runs `dotnet test` (`release.yml:98-123`). So PR-4 must keep `Fixtures/Generators/**` excluded from the test project (`tests/turnkey-sdk-csharp.Tests.csproj:23-26` currently copies all fixtures), and PR-13 must add `actions/setup-node` for the generator workflow.

Monthly drift issue creation is bounded for issue count: the YAML searches an existing open issue by label and package, edits it if found, creates only if absent (`plans/...:441-463`). It can still add one comment per month, but not infinite issues.

Platform-agnostic claim is acceptable for the proposed purejs generator path: the relevant dependencies are JS packages in `package.json` (`@noble/*`, `borsh`, `cbor-js`, `@peculiar/x509`) and Node built-in crypto is only for non-byte-stable paths. No native module or WASM dependency is evident in the pinned package manifests.

**F. Plan Writing Quality**

Blocking writing issues remain:

- PR-4 is not independently mergeable as written in the PR table because it omits the csproj exclusion needed to keep generators out of `dotnet test`.
- PR-14 dependency should mention conditional PR-9b.
- PR-1 title says v2 despite the plan being v3.
- Must-have goals are mostly measurable, but Drift detection has contradictory pass/fail semantics and must be normalized.
- Redundancy is acceptable except HPKE/QOS wording, which is not merely redundant; it reintroduces the v2 confusion in Sections 3 and 13.

**G. Unresolved Assumptions**

Could not verify these in this round:

- Other-language SDK fixture claims across `tkhq/sdk` / `swift-sdk` / `dart-sdk` / `go-sdk` / `rust-sdk` at `plans/...:161-184` and references `657-662`; only local pinned TS snapshots were available.
- `peak/` grep claims for proof and `withAsyncPolling` usage at lines 21, 292, 607-608, and 625; this worktree does not contain the peak monorepo.
- `tkhq/python-sdk` being the only SDK with live backend e2e at lines 183-184.
- PR-7a fixed-ephemeral injection feasibility at lines 401-411; the plan correctly defers it, but it remains unverified.

Round 2 PASS criterion is not met: B has rows, C has corrections, E is bounded after fixes but not yet internally consistent, and F has blocking writing issues.
